                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=10411">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Cervelli, who was shut down in August due to an assortment of injuries, is healthy heading into spring training, the Pittsburgh Tribune-Review reports. "I feel good and ready to go," the catcher said Tuesday. (2/14/2018)</div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>With Jorge Posada creeping up on 40 and suffering from foot, knee and shoulder ailments, Cervelli saw significant time behind the plate for the Yankees in 2010. The Venezuelan-born backstop of Italian descent batted .271/.359/.335 in more than 300 plate appearances, putting up a .315 wOBA. On the positive side, Cervelli worked pitchers for a walk in 10.4% of his PA, swinging at just 21.3% of pitches thrown off the plate (29.3% MLB average). But, the catcher with a career .380 minor-league slugging percentage didn't give Yankees announcer Michael Kay a single opportunity to bellow "See Ya!" Cervelli didn't go deep in 2010, and his .064 ISO ranked in the bottom 15 among hitters with 300+ PA. Batters with little thump see more fastballs, and Cervelli got one nearly 67% of the time. Per 100 fastballs seen, he was about six-tenths of a run below average. Cervelli's walk rate could fall some if pitchers challenge him more often. He's still got a decent bat by catching standards, but the Yankees appear intent on giving towering prospect Jesus Montero a chance to stick at catcher, and Austin Romine is another potential regular close behind. Posada's supposed to DH more in 2011, but it's not clear if Cervelli will pick up more playing time.  (David Golebiewski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Cervelli's plate approach figures to afford him a long big-league career, but he's not a premium young talent. In New York, he's keeping home plate warm for one of the Yankees' top catching prospects. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Even on a run-augmenting team like the Yankees, the backup catcher is not usually fantasy relevant. Then you have to add in the fact that the Yankees have Austin Romine and Jesus Montero coming up behind Russ Martin, too.  (Eno Sarris)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>If Francisco Cervelli is ever going to be given another chance to be a starting catcher, it will have to be on team other than the Yankees. Cervelli had a disastrous 2013 season which was marred with injuries and a suspension related to the Biogenesis scandal. Now that the Yankees have brought in Brian McCann for the next five years, Cervelli has been relegated to competing against Austin Romine and J.R. Murphy to be the backup. He does have a respectable .271 career batting average, but that is only through 542 at bats spanning parts of six seasons. Even if he does emerge as the Yankees' second catcher, he will not produce anywhere enough to make him worth rostering. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/FantasyJudgment">Michael A. Stein</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Given his age, injury history, and connection with Biogenesis, it seems likely that the Yankees would opt for a younger and more defensive-oriented backup such as Romine or Murphy. If they go in that direction, there is a chance Cervelli could end up on another team which might increase his value enough to consider rostering him in very deep leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Cervelli, who turns 29 in March, will get the first opportunity of his career to be a first-string catcher after he was traded from the Yankees to the Pirates in November. Acquired mainly for his defense and framing ability, Cervelli has compiled a respectable .278 average over his 785 big league plate appearances, with a .781 on-base plus slugging percentage against southpaws. He offers little in the way of pop, however, evidenced by a career .103 isolated power mark and 10 career home runs. It also probably won’t help that he’s leaving the hitter-friendly Yankee Stadium for PNC Park, a place that typically leans toward favoring pitchers. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Karl_de_Vries">Karl de Vries</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>We’ll see how Cervelli fares in his first full major league season, but it would seem he has little value beyond deep two-catcher formats.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>At 29, Francisco Cervelli experienced a late-career breakout of sorts, taking the Pittsburgh Pirates' catching gig and running with it. Aside from marginal defensive acumen, Cervelli makes his money playing the batted ball game -- his career .341 batting average on balls in play generates the vast majority of his offensive value. For a catcher who neither runs nor hits for power, he leaves little margin for error and generates somewhat empty fantasy value. Then again, most catchers generate empty fantasy value, so it's hard to complain. Cervelli's expected playing time -- he figures to dominate the Pirates' backstop gig again -- makes him a mid-range starting catcher in NL-only leagues and a back-end number one in deep mixed leagues. Preferably, he would be drafted as a good second backstop in two-catcher leagues and a solid backup everywhere else, where bench space permits. It's just difficult to rely on one-category production that depends heavily on a peripheral metric that can be so volatile, and especially if said metric has, for whatever reason, overstated Cervelli's skill level. Because if the BABIP crashes down to Earth, so, too, will Cervelli. (Alex Chamberlain)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Francisco Cervelli figures to see the majority of playing time among Pirates catchers but offers mostly one-category production that depends heavily on batted ball luck. He best serves fantasy squads in deep formats but could make for a decent backup in standard leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>To start for the Yankees, one must have a certain degree of excellence. At least, that was the case back when the Yankees employed Cervelli. Although 'excellence' doesn't really apply to Cervelli's work, he is rather good. And good players can start for the Pirates. Thus, it was providential that the Pirates acquired (ahem, stole) Cervelli prior to the 2015 season. Since then, he's recorded 5.5 WAR and signed a three-year, $31 million contract extension through 2019. Cervelli regressed in a bad way during the 2016 campaign, however. He hit just one home run in 393 plate appearances. Fortunately, a lofty .377 on-base percentage buoyed otherwise indifferent work at the plate. Injuries also interrupted his season. Cervelli is poised to experience the good type of regression in 2017, perhaps hitting as many as five(!) home runs. With that in mind, he is not a particularly exciting option in fantasy. (Brad Johnson)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>While everybody else hit 20 home runs in 2016, Cervelli said, "nah, I'll settle for one." Perhaps he'll take a few meatier swings in 2017. He's a league-average catcher so long as long as he keeps walking.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
